# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Kubernetes Server-Side Apply Configuration Guide

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a deep guide for applyconfigurations and Server-Side Apply semantics, including conflict handling and workflow patterns.

## Scope

Focus on the applyconfigurations and Server-Side Apply subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

106-assistanttext-
The documentation has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what the guide covers:

---

**Structure of the document:**

1. **Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies** — explains SSA as a declarative field-ownership protocol, identifies the two halves (client-side `applyconfigurations` types and the server-side `managedfields` engine), and maps upstream (`sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff`, `kube-openapi`) and downstream (`apiserver/handlers/patch.go`, generated typed clients, CRD handler) dependencies.

2. **Key Components and Responsibility Split** — documents all nine layers of the `Manager` decorator chain assembled in `NewDefaultFieldManager` (from `versionCheckManager` at the outermost to `structuredMergeManager` at the innermost), `TypeConverter` and its three implementations, the `GvkParser` / `internal.go` schema blob, the generated `*ApplyConfiguration` pointer-field structs, and `ScaleHandler`.

3. **End-to-End Control Flow** — traces a complete SSA request from HTTP arrival (`PatchResource`), through the `GuaranteedUpdate` retry loop, into `FieldManager.Apply`, into `structuredMergeManager.Apply` calling `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff`, and back out through `EncodeObjectManagedFields`. Also covers the non-apply update path and the client-side `Apply` function workflow.

4. **Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs** — covers conflict errors and their structure, the `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10` cap, managedFields removal on size overflow, duplicate-field handling, the no-op write optimisation, version-less applier identity, schemeless CRD limitations, and subresource field isolation.

5. **Extension Points, Customisation Hooks, and Risks** — covers custom `TypeConverter` injection, `resetFields` filters, `Scale
... (truncated)

If no managed fields are found for the given fieldManager,\\n34: // no error is returned, but applyConfiguration is left unpopulated. It is possible\\n35: // that no managed fields were found for the fieldManager because other field managers\\n36: // have taken ownership of all the fields previously owned by the fieldManager. It is\\n37: // also possible the fieldManager never owned fields.\\n38: //\\n39: // The provided object MUST bo a root resource object since subresource objects\\n40: // do not contain their own managed fields. For example, an autoscaling.Scale\\n41: // object read from a \\\"scale\\\" subresource does not have any managed fields and so\\n42: // cannot be used as the object.\\n43: //\\n44: // If the fields of a subresource are a subset of the fields of the root object,\\n45: // and their field paths and types are exactly the same, then ExtractInto can be\\n46: // called with the root resource as the object and the subresource as the\\n47: // applyConfiguration. This works for \\\"status\\\", obviously, because status is\\n48: // represented by the exact same object as the root resource. This does NOT\\n49: // work, for example, with the \\\"scale\\\" subresources of Deployment, ReplicaSet and\\n50: // StatefulSet.     "content": "1: /*\n2: Copyright 2021 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: package managedfields\n18: \n19: import (\n20: \t\"bytes\"\n21: \t\"fmt\"\n22: \n23: \t\"sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6/fieldpath\"\n24: \t\"sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6/typed\"\n25: \n26: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/meta\"\n27: \tmetav1 \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1\"\n28: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1/unstructured\"\n29: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime\"\n30: )\n31: \n32: // ExtractInto extracts the applied configuration state from object for fieldManager\n33: // into applyConfiguration. If no managed fields are found for the given fieldManager,\n34: // no error is returned, but applyConfiguration is left unpopulated. It is possible\n35: // that no managed fields were found for the fieldManager because other field managers\n36: // have taken ownership of all the fields previously owned by the fieldManager. It is\n37: // also possible the fieldManager never owned fields.\n38: //\n39: // The provided object MUST bo a root resource object since subresource objects\n40: // do not contain their own managed fields. For example, an autoscaling.Scale\n41: // object read from a \"scale\" subresource does not have any managed fields and so\n42: // cannot be used as the object.\n43: //\n44: // If the fields of a subresource are a subset of the fields of the root object,\n45: // and their field paths and types are exactly the same, then ExtractInto can be\n46: // called with the root resource as the object and the subresource as the\n47: // applyConfiguration. This does NOT\n49: // work, for example, with the \"scale\" subresources of Deployment, ReplicaSet and\n50: // StatefulSet. \"k\"\n42: \n43: \t// Separator separates the type of a path element from the contents\n44: \tSeparator = \":\"\n45: )\n46: \n47: // NewPathElement parses a serialized path element\n48: func NewPathElement(s string) (fieldpath.PathElement, error) {\n49: \tsplit := strings.SplitN(s, Separator, 2)\n50: \tif len(split) < 2 {\n51: \t\treturn fieldpath.PathElement{}, fmt.Errorf(\"missing 51. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Server-Side Apply and applyconfigurations: A Deep Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative ownership and merge protocol for Kubernetes objects. Rather than replacing a whole object or computing a diff client-side, SSA lets each actor (called a *field manager*) declare the fields it owns. The API server stores these ownership claims per-field in `metadata.managedFields`, and enforces them on every subsequent write.\n\nThe protocol has two tightly coupled halves:\n\n| Half | Location | Role |\n|------|----------|------|\n| **applyconfigurations** (client-side types) | `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Typed, pointer-field Go structs used to build SSA requests |\n| **managedfields engine** (server-side processing) | `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/` | Receives patch, performs merge, updates ownership |\n\n### Upstream dependencies\n\n- **`sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6`** (`merge`, `typed`, `fieldpath` packages): the authoritative merge algorithm. Kubernetes does not implement the ownership logic directly; it delegates to this external library.\n- **`k8s.io/kube-openapi`** (`schemaconv`, `proto`): converts Kubernetes OpenAPI models into the schema format that `structured-merge-diff` understands. Without it, `TypeConverter` cannot annotate objects with structural type information.\n- **`k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1`**: `ManagedFieldsEntry`, `PatchOptions`, `ApplyOptions` \u2014 the wire types carried in API objects and requests.\n\n### Downstream consumers\n\n- **`k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`**: the HTTP `PATCH` handler; routes `application/apply-patch+yaml` (and CBOR) requests to the SSA path.\n- **`k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/typed/\u2026`**: generated typed clients whose `Apply` methods accept `*ApplyConfiguration` objects and call the API server with `ApplyPatchType`.\n- **CRD handler** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/apiserver/customresource_handler.go`): uses `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` for CRD-scoped field management.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 The `Manager` decorator chain\n\nThe engine is assembled as a nested chain of `Manager` decorators inside `NewDefaultFieldManager` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go:57`):\n\n```go\nNewVersionCheckManager(\n  NewLastAppliedUpdater(\n    NewLastAppliedManager(\n      NewProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager(\n        NewCapManagersManager(\n          NewBuildManagerInfoManager(\n            NewManagedFieldsUpdater(\n              NewStripMetaManager(f),  // f = structuredMergeManager\n            ),\n          ),\n        ),\n      ),\n    ),\n  ),\n)\n```\n\nEach layer wraps the previous one and performs a single focused responsibility:\n\n| Layer | File | Purpose |\n|-------|------|---------|\n| `versionCheckManager` | `internal/versioncheck.go` | Rejects apply requests whose `GVK` does not match the endpoint's registered kind |\n| `lastAppliedUpdater` | `internal/lastappliedupdater.go` | On `kubectl` apply, mirrors the final object back into `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation for backward compat |\n| `lastAppliedManager` | `internal/lastappliedmanager.go` | During a `kubectl` SSA, detects conflicts that overlap with fields the client previously owned via CSA, and transparently force-applies those fields to avoid blocking the upgrade path |\n| `skipNonAppliedManager` (probabilistic) | `internal/skipnonapplied.go` | Skips field tracking on update-only objects until the first apply is seen; initialises tracking for creates with a configurable probability (`DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability = 1`) |\n| `capManagersManager` | `internal/capmanagers.go` | Limits update-sourced manager entries to `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10` by merging the oldest into a `\"ancient-changes\"` bucket |\n| `buildManagerInfoManager` | `internal/buildmanagerinfo.go` | Normalises the manager identifier into a stable JSON string (`{\"manager\":\u2026,\"operation\":\u2026,\"apiVersion\":\u2026,\"subresource\":\u2026}`) \u2014 for appliers the `apiVersion` is omitted so the manager key stays constant across version bumps |\n| `managedFieldsUpdater` | `internal/managedfieldsupdater.go` | Sets the timestamp on the manager entry after a successful write; for updates, detects field changes by running the inner merge under a sentinel `\"current-operation\"` key, then transfers ownership to the real manager |\n| `stripMetaManager` | `internal/stripmeta.go` | Removes immutable meta-fields (`apiVersion`, `kind`, `metadata.name`, `metadata.namespace`, `metadata.managedFields`, etc.) from all field-sets so they are never tracked |\n| `structuredMergeManager` | `internal/structuredmerge.go` | **Core leaf**: converts runtime objects to `typed.TypedValue`, calls `merge.Updater.Apply` or `merge.Updater.Update` from `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6` |\n\n### 2.2 `FieldManager` (top-level)\n\n`FieldManager` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:45`) is the public surface. It exposes:\n\n- `Update(liveObj, newObj, manager)` \u2014 called for non-apply writes (create, update, patch) to track field ownership without performing a merge.\n- `Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, manager, force)` \u2014 called for SSA apply requests; delegates into the chain and converts `merge.Conflicts` into `StatusError` with `CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict`.\n- `UpdateNoErrors(liveObj, newObj, manager)` \u2014 a fault-tolerant wrapper for `Update`; on error, clears `managedFields` rather than propagating (used by `jsonPatcher` and `smpPatcher` in the HTTP handler).\n\n### 2.3 TypeConverter\n\n`TypeConverter` (`internal/typeconverter.go:34`) bridges `runtime.Object` and `typed.TypedValue`:\n\n```go\ntype TypeConverter interface {\n    ObjectToTyped(runtime.Object, ...typed.ValidationOptions) (*typed.TypedValue, error)\n    TypedToObject(*typed.TypedValue) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\nThree implementations exist:\n\n- `typeConverter` \u2014 for built-in resources; uses a `map[GVK]*typed.ParseableType` built from the kube-openapi spec via `schemaconv.ToSchemaFromOpenAPI`.\n- `deducedTypeConverter` \u2014 for schemeless CRDs; uses `typed.DeducedParseableType`, which treats every list as atomic and every map as granular.\n- `schemeTypeConverter` \u2014 added in 2025 (`runtimetypeconverter.go`); uses the runtime `Scheme` to look up the OpenAPI definition name, allowing type conversion without a pre-built schema map.\n\n### 2.4 `GvkParser` and `internal.go` schema blob\n\n`GvkParser` (`managedfields/gvkparser.go`) maps a `GroupVersionKind` to a named type in the SMD schema, indexed from `proto.Models`.\n\nOn the client side, `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/internal/internal.go` contains a **generated** `typed.YAMLObject` schema blob for all built-in Kubernetes resource types. The `Parser()` singleton builds a `typed.Parser` from this blob once per process. Each generated per-type `Extract*` function calls `internal.Parser().Type(\"io.k8s.api.apps.v1.Deployment\")` to obtain the correct `typed.ParseableType` for extraction.\n\n### 2.5 Apply Configuration types\n\nUnder `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/<group>/<version>/` every Kubernetes kind has a generated `*ApplyConfiguration` struct (e.g., `DeploymentApplyConfiguration`). These differ from the canonical API types in one important way: **every field is a pointer** (including scalars), so that `omitempty` on JSON marshalling means \"not set by this actor\" rather than \"zero value\". This makes intent unambiguous: a nil field is absent from the apply request; the server retains whatever value is already there.\n\nTwo generated functions accompany each type:\n\n```go\n// Build from scratch\nfunc Deployment(name, namespace string) *DeploymentApplyConfiguration\n\n// Extract from live object (extract/modify-in-place/apply pattern)\nfunc ExtractDeployment(deployment *appsv1.Deployment, fieldManager string) (*DeploymentApplyConfiguration, error)\nfunc ExtractDeploymentFrom(deployment *appsv1.Deployment, fieldManager, subresource string) (*DeploymentApplyConfiguration, error)\n```\n\n`ExtractDeployment` delegates to `managedfields.ExtractInto` in `extract.go`, which reads the `FieldsV1` bitset for the named manager, calls `typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves())` via SMD, and deserialises the resulting unstructured map into the `*ApplyConfiguration` target.\n\n### 2.6 `ScaleHandler`\n\n`ScaleHandler` (`managedfields/scalehandler.go`) is a translation adapter for subresources whose field-paths differ from the parent resource. When reading `spec.replicas` through the `scale` subresource, the field is at `spec.replicas` in the parent but at `spec.replicas` in `autoscaling/v1.Scale`. `ToSubresource` projects the parent's managed field entries to the scale representation, and `ToParent` propagates changes back.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 HTTP request arrival\n\nAn SSA request arrives as `PATCH /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments/myapp` with `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml`.\n\n`PatchResource` (`handlers/patch.go:68`) reads the body, validates options, wraps admission, then dispatches on patch type:\n\n```go\ncase types.ApplyYAMLPatchType:\n    p.mechanism = newApplyPatcher(p, scope.FieldManager, yaml.Unmarshal, yaml.UnmarshalStrict)\n    p.forceAllowCreate = true\n```\n\nThe `scope.FieldManager` is a `*managedfields.FieldManager` wired up at endpoint installation time; it encapsulates the full decorator chain.\n\n### 3.2 GuaranteedUpdate loop\n\n`patchResource` sets up a transformer pipeline:\n\n```go\ntransformers := []rest.TransformFunc{p.applyPatch, p.applyAdmission, dedupOwnerReferences}\np.updatedObjectInfo = rest.DefaultUpdatedObjectInfo(nil, transformers...)\nrequestFunc = func() { p.restPatcher.Update(ctx, name, p.updatedObjectInfo, ...) }\n```\n\n`restPatcher.Update` (e.g., the generic registry's `Update`) calls `GuaranteedUpdate`, which retries the whole pipeline on conflict. On each attempt:\n\n1. **`p.applyPatch`** is called with the current live object from storage.\n2. Inside `applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject` (`patch.go:500`), the YAML body is unmarshalled into an `unstructured.Unstructured`.\n3. `p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, fieldManager, force)` is called.\n\n### 3.3 Inside `FieldManager.Apply`\n\n`FieldManager.Apply` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:183`):\n\n1. Decodes `liveObj.managedFields` via `DecodeManagedFields` into a `ManagedInterface` (a `fieldpath.ManagedFields` map + timestamp map).\n2. Calls through the decorator chain, bottom of which is `structuredMergeManager.Apply`.\n3. If the result is a `merge.Conflicts`, wraps it in a `StatusError` (`NewConflictError` in `internal/conflict.go`) with per-field `StatusCause` entries.\n4. On success, encodes the updated `ManagedInterface` back into `object.metadata.managedFields` via `EncodeObjectManagedFields`.\n\n### 3.4 Inside `structuredMergeManager.Apply`\n\n`structuredMergeManager.Apply` (`internal/structuredmerge.go:121`):\n\n1. Validates that the apply object's `GVK` matches the endpoint version.\n2. Rejects a non-nil `managedFields` in the patch object (clients may not set it).\n3. Converts `liveObj` to `typed.TypedValue` (allowing duplicates) and `patchObj` to `typed.TypedValue` (strict, no duplicates).\n4. Calls `f.updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion, managed.Fields(), manager, force)` \u2014 `f.updater` is a `merge.Updater` from `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6/merge`, which implements ownership semantics.\n5. Converts the resulting `*typed.TypedValue` back to `runtime.Object`, runs the object defaulter, and converts to the hub version.\n\n### 3.5 Conflict detection and force-apply\n\n`merge.Updater.Apply` returns `merge.Conflicts` when the incoming patch claims ownership of a field currently owned by a *different* manager. The `force` flag, passed from the client via `PatchOptions.Force`, bypasses this check and transfers ownership.\n\nThe `lastAppliedManager` layer intercepts conflicts on `kubectl` apply and filters them against fields present in `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration`: if a conflict falls entirely within the previously-owned CSA set, it silently re-applies with `force=true`. This is the migration path from client-side apply to SSA (`internal/lastappliedmanager.go:59-88`).\n\n### 3.6 Update path (non-apply writes)\n\nFor regular creates, updates, and non-apply patches, `FieldManager.Update` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:120`) is used instead of `Apply`. The `decodeLiveOrNew` helper resolves which `managedFields` to use as the starting point (live object for subresources, new object for full updates). `structuredMergeManager.Update` calls `f.updater.Update`, which tracks field changes without performing ownership merges or raising conflicts.\n\nThe `managedFieldsUpdater` layer uses a sentinel manager `\"current-operation\"` to detect whether any fields actually changed before assigning a new timestamp \u2014 an optimization preventing timestamp churn when a write is a no-op with respect to fields.\n\n### 3.7 Client-side flow: Apply functions\n\n```go\n// From doc.go example\nhpaApplyConfig := autoscalingv1.HorizontalPodAutoscaler(\"myHPA\", \"myNamespace\").\n    WithSpec(autoscalingv1.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec().\n        WithMinReplicas(1).\n        WithMaxReplicas(10).\n        WithMetrics(...)\n    )\nhpav1client.Apply(ctx, hpaApplyConfig, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"mycontroller\", Force: true})\n```\n\nThe generated `Apply` method on the typed client serialises the `*ApplyConfiguration` as JSON (with `omitempty` eliding nil fields), sends a `PATCH` with `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml`, and sets `?fieldManager=mycontroller&force=true` in the query string. The server receives only the fields explicitly set by the client.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Conflict errors\n\nA non-force apply that conflicts returns HTTP 409 with:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"message\": \"Apply failed with 2 conflicts: conflicts with \\\"other-controller\\\":\\n- .spec.replicas\\n- .spec.selector\",\n  \"status\": \"Failure\",\n  \"reason\": \"Conflict\",\n  \"details\": {\n    \"causes\": [\n      { \"reason\": \"FieldManagerConflict\", \"message\": \"conflict with \\\"other-controller\\\"\", \"field\": \".spec.replicas\" }\n    ]\n  }\n}\n```\n\nThe error is built in `internal/conflict.go:33`. Callers should inspect `errors.IsConflict(err)` and either back off, use `Force: true`, or change field ownership design.\n\n### 4.2 Manager entry cap\n\n`capManagersManager` limits update-manager entries to `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:35`). When exceeded, oldest entries (by timestamp) are merged into a per-version `\"ancient-changes\"` bucket (`internal/capmanagers.go:92`). This prevents unbounded growth of `managedFields` at the cost of losing attribution for old changes. Controllers that update objects frequently under rotating manager names (e.g., including a timestamp in the manager name) will hit this cap rapidly.\n\n### 4.3 Size pressure and managedFields removal\n\nIf an object exceeds the etcd value size limit, `patchResource` retries without `managedFields` for non-apply patch types (`patch.go:713-725`). This fallback is explicitly *not* applied to `ApplyYAMLPatchType` or `ApplyCBORPatchType` because apply semantics require the field set to be present.\n\n### 4.4 Duplicate fields\n\n`structuredMergeManager.Update` converts the live object with `typed.AllowDuplicates` because etcd may hold objects with duplicate keys (legacy data). Apply requests do not allow duplicates and fail immediately if the patch contains them (`structuredmerge.go:145`).\n\n### 4.5 No-op write optimisation\n\n`IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer` (`handlers/fieldmanager/equality.go:114`) is a write transformer that, after all mutations and admission, checks whether the only change in the new object is a timestamp bump in `managedFields`. If the object content is otherwise identical (using custom equality that ignores timestamps), the timestamps are reverted to prevent spurious `resourceVersion` increments and etcd writes. The check is opt-out via the env var `KUBE_APISERVER_AVOID_NOOP_SSA_TIMESTAMP_UPDATES=false`.\n\n### 4.6 Version-less applier identity\n\n`buildManagerInfoManager.buildManagerInfo` omits `APIVersion` from the manager key for apply operations (`buildmanagerinfo.go:63-73`). This means `kubectl` remains the same owner across a `apps/v1beta1` \u2192 `apps/v1` API version migration. Update entries, by contrast, include the API version, forming a per-version ownership footprint.\n\n### 4.7 CRD field tracking without schema\n\nFor CRDs without an OpenAPI schema, `deducedTypeConverter` treats all lists as atomic and all maps as granular. This means list items are not individually trackable; an apply that changes any list item replaces the entire list. Once a schema is added (with appropriate list-type annotations), the tracking improves. This is a fundamental limitation of schema-free CRDs.\n\n### 4.8 Subresource field isolation\n\n`FieldManager` is constructed with a `subresource` string. For subresource writes, `decodeLiveOrNew` always uses the live object's `managedFields` rather than whatever the client submits (`fieldmanager.go:83-87`). This prevents a subresource write from overwriting or corrupting the main resource's field ownership.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customisation Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 5.1 `TypeConverter` injection\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` and `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` both accept a `TypeConverter` argument. Third-party API extensions can supply their own implementation of:\n\n```go\ntype TypeConverter interface {\n    ObjectToTyped(runtime.Object, ...typed.ValidationOptions) (*typed.TypedValue, error)\n    TypedToObject(*typed.TypedValue) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\nThe `schemeTypeConverter` (`internal/runtimetypeconverter.go`) introduced in 2025 is an example; it uses `runtime.Scheme.ToOpenAPIDefinitionName` to look up the schema type, making it easier to wire SSA without a full OpenAPI spec map at construction time.\n\n**Risk**: an incorrect `TypeConverter` that misreports field types or allows unknown fields will silently corrupt ownership tracking or bypass conflict detection.\n\n### 5.2 `resetFields` filter\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` accepts a `map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter` as `resetFields`. Fields matching a filter are excluded from ownership tracking on update. This is used, for example, to prevent the apiserver from claiming ownership of fields that are reset to defaults on every write (e.g., `status` fields managed by a controller). Incorrectly configured filters can cause fields to appear unowned, allowing any applier to claim them silently.\n\n### 5.3 `ScaleHandler` for custom subresources\n\nAggregated API servers and CRD conversion webhooks that expose custom `scale` subresources use `ScaleHandler.ToSubresource` / `ToParent` to bridge field ownership between the custom resource schema and the `autoscaling/v1.Scale` schema. Registering incorrect `ResourcePathMappings` will cause replicas-ownership attribution to be lost on scale operations.\n\n### 5.4 CSA\u2192SSA upgrade utilities\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/csaupgrade/upgrade.go` provides `UpgradeManagedFields` and `UpgradeManagedFieldsPatch` for controllers migrating from client-side apply (kubectl `last-applied-configuration`) to SSA. The operation converts `Update`-operation entries for named managers into `Apply`-operation entries under a new SSA manager name. **This operation is irreversible**: the original field-level provenance is lost. Care must be taken to apply the resulting patch before any other concurrent writer changes the object.\n\n### 5.5 `UnstructuredExtractor` for dynamic clients\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/meta/v1/unstructured.go` provides an `UnstructuredExtractor` that fetches the live OpenAPI schema via discovery, builds a `GvkParser` with a 1-minute TTL, and calls `ExtractInto` to produce an `*unstructured.Unstructured` scoped to one field manager. This is the primary extension point for dynamic controllers that do not have generated typed clients.\n\n**Risk**: the TTL cache means schema changes (e.g., CRD version additions) may not be reflected immediately, causing `Extract` to use an outdated field set for up to 1 minute.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance\n\n**Object size growth**: `managedFields` in `metadata` grows with the number of distinct field managers. A single `kubectl apply` on a Deployment can add 2\u20133 KB of `managedFields` JSON. With `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10`, update churn from many distinct agents is bounded but not eliminated.\n\n**Per-request schema parsing**: The `typeConverter` is built once per `FieldManager` instance (one per kind per server) from the OpenAPI spec. During schema reloads (CRD updates), all in-flight apply operations for that kind must wait for the new `TypeConverter` to be constructed. The `schemeTypeConverter` variant avoids this by delegating to the live `Scheme`.\n\n**SMD merge complexity**: The `merge.Updater.Apply` call is O(fields \u00d7 managers). For objects with hundreds of fields and tens of managers (e.g., large Pods managed by many admission mutators), apply latency is measurable. The `CapManagersManager` is the principal mitigation.\n\n**No-op write suppression**: `IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer` prevents the common case of \"apply the same config on every reconcile loop\" from generating etcd writes, which is critical at scale.\n\n### 6.2 Reliability\n\n**`UpdateNoErrors`**: For non-apply patch types, managed field tracking failures are silently absorbed (clearing `managedFields`) rather than blocking the write. This means a storage-size-triggered or SMD-parse-triggered error degrades tracking gracefully but leaves the object without ownership information, which cannot be recovered automatically.\n\n**GuaranteedUpdate retry**: The entire `applyPatch \u2192 applyAdmission \u2192 dedup` pipeline runs inside `GuaranteedUpdate`'s retry loop. A conflict-prone object (one with many competing SSA writers) can cause many retries. Controllers should use `Force: true` and stable manager names to minimise retry pressure.\n\n### 6.3 Maintainability\n\n**Code generation**: Almost all files under `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/<group>/<version>/` and the `utils.go` dispatch table are generated by `applyconfiguration-gen`. The source of truth is the `k8s.io/api` type definitions and their JSON tags. Adding a new API field requires regenerating these packages. Handwriting an apply configuration type is an error-prone alternative.\n\n**Schema blob in `internal.go`**: The `schemaYAML` constant in `internal/internal.go` is a verbatim embedded copy of the SMD schema for all built-in types. It is regenerated as part of the release process and can become stale if the API types change between regenerations. The consequence is that `ExtractInto` may silently omit new fields that are not yet in the embedded schema.\n\n---\n\n## 7. File and Directory Map\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 internal/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 internal.go                    # Embedded SMD schema blob; Parser() singleton\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 meta/v1/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 managedfieldsentry.go          # ManagedFieldsEntryApplyConfiguration\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 unstructured.go                # UnstructuredExtractor (gvkParserCache + ExtractInto)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apps/v1/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 deployment.go                  # DeploymentApplyConfiguration; ExtractDeployment\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 utils.go                           # Dispatch table: For(obj) \u2192 *ApplyConfiguration\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 doc.go                             # (excluded by anti-requirements)\n\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 fieldmanager.go                    # Public NewDefaultFieldManager / NewDefaultCRDFieldManager\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 extract.go                         # ExtractInto: core extract-from-live logic\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 gvkparser.go                       # GvkParser: GVK \u2192 typed.ParseableType from proto.Models\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 typeconverter.go                   # TypeConverter interface re-export; NewTypeConverter, NewSchemeTypeConverter\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 scalehandler.go                    # ScaleHandler: translate managedFields for /scale subresource\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 internal/\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 manager.go                     # Manager interface (Update + Apply)\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 fieldmanager.go                # FieldManager struct; Apply / Update / UpdateNoErrors; decodeLiveOrNew\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 structuredmerge.go             # structuredMergeManager: calls sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 typeconverter.go               # typeConverter (OpenAPI-backed); deducedTypeConverter\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 runtimetypeconverter.go        # schemeTypeConverter (Scheme-backed, 2025)\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 versionconverter.go            # versionConverter: adapts runtime.ObjectConvertor for SMD\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 managedfields.go               # Encode/DecodeManagedFields; BuildManagerIdentifier\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 managedfieldsupdater.go        # managedFieldsUpdater: timestamp and delta-based ownership update\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 buildmanagerinfo.go            # buildManagerInfoManager: normalise manager key\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 capmanagers.go                 # capManagersManager: cap update entries at 10; \"ancient-changes\"\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 skipnonapplied.go              # skipNonAppliedManager: probabilistic tracking enablement\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 lastappliedmanager.go          # lastAppliedManager: CSA\u2192SSA upgrade during kubectl apply\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 lastappliedupdater.go          # lastAppliedUpdater: keep last-applied annotation in sync\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 stripmeta.go                   # stripMetaManager: exclude immutable meta fields\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 versioncheck.go                # versionCheckManager: reject wrong-version apply objects\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 conflict.go                    # NewConflictError: build StatusError from merge.Conflicts\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 pathelement.go                 # PathElement serialisation (f:, v:, k:, i: prefixes)\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 fields.go                      # FieldsToSet / SetToFields: FieldsV1 \u2194 fieldpath.Set\n\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 patch.go                           # PatchResource HTTP handler; patcher; applyPatcher; smpPatcher; jsonPatcher\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 fieldmanager/\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 equality.go                    # IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer; no-op write suppression\n\nstaging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/csaupgrade/\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 upgrade.go                         # UpgradeManagedFields / UpgradeManagedFieldsPatch: CSA\u2192SSA migration\n```\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"

{
  "content": "# Server-Side Apply and applyconfigurations: A Deep Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative ownership and merge protocol for Kubernetes objects. Rather than replacing a whole object or computing a diff client-side, SSA lets each actor (called a *field manager*) declare the fields it owns. The API server stores these ownership claims per-field in `metadata.managedFields`, and enforces them on every subsequent write.\n\nThe protocol has two tightly coupled halves:\n\n| Half | Location | Role |\n|------|----------|------|\n| **applyconfigurations** (client-side types) | `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Typed, pointer-field Go structs used to build SSA requests |\n| **managedfields engine** (server-side processing) | `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/` | Receives patch, performs merge, updates ownership |\n\n### Upstream dependencies\n\n- **`sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6`** (`merge`, `typed`, `fieldpath` packages): the authoritative merge algorithm. Kubernetes does not implement the ownership logic directly; it delegates to this external library.\n- **`k8s.io/kube-openapi`** (`schemaconv`, `proto`): converts Kubernetes OpenAPI models into the schema format that `structured-merge-diff` understands. Without it, `TypeConverter` cannot annotate objects with structural type information.\n- **`k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1`**: `ManagedFieldsEntry`, `PatchOptions`, `ApplyOptions` \u2014 the wire types carried in API objects and requests.\n\n### Downstream consumers\n\n- **`k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`**: the HTTP `PATCH` handler; routes `application/apply-patch+yaml` (and CBOR) requests to the SSA path.\n- **`k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/typed/\u2026`**: generated typed clients whose `Apply` methods accept `*ApplyConfiguration` objects and call the API server with `ApplyPatchType`.\n- **CRD handler** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/apiserver/customresource_handler.go`): uses `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` for CRD-scoped field management.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 The `Manager` decorator chain\n\nThe engine is assembled as a nested chain of `Manager` decorators inside `NewDefaultFieldManager` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go:57`):\n\n```go\nNewVersionCheckManager(\n  NewLastAppliedUpdater(\n    NewLastAppliedManager(\n      NewProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager(\n        NewCapManagersManager(\n          NewBuildManagerInfoManager(\n            NewManagedFieldsUpdater(\n              NewStripMetaManager(f),  // f = structuredMergeManager\n            ),\n          ),\n        ),\n      ),\n    ),\n  ),\n)\n```\n\nEach layer wraps the previous one and performs a single focused responsibility:\n\n| Layer | File | Purpose |\n|-------|------|---------|\n| `versionCheckManager` | `internal/versioncheck.go` | Rejects apply requests whose `GVK` does not match the endpoint's registered kind |\n| `lastAppliedUpdater` | `internal/lastappliedupdater.go` | On `kubectl` apply, mirrors the final object back into `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation for backward compat |\n| `lastAppliedManager` | `internal/lastappliedmanager.go` | During a `kubectl` SSA, detects conflicts that overlap with fields the client previously owned via CSA, and transparently force-applies those fields to avoid blocking the upgrade path |\n| `skipNonAppliedManager` (probabilistic) | `internal/skipnonapplied.go` | Skips field tracking on update-only objects until the first apply is seen; initialises tracking for creates with a configurable probability (`DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability = 1`) |\n| `capManagersManager` | `internal/capmanagers.go` | Limits update-sourced manager entries to `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10` by merging the oldest into a `\"ancient-changes\"` bucket |\n| `buildManagerInfoManager` | `internal/buildmanagerinfo.go` | Normalises the manager identifier into a stable JSON string (`{\"manager\":\u2026,\"operation\":\u2026,\"apiVersion\":\u2026,\"subresource\":\u2026}`) \u2014 for appliers the `apiVersion` is omitted so the manager key stays constant across version bumps |\n| `managedFieldsUpdater` | `internal/managedfieldsupdater.go` | Sets the timestamp on the manager entry after a successful write; for updates, detects field changes by running the inner merge under a sentinel `\"current-operation\"` key, then transfers ownership to the real manager |\n| `stripMetaManager` | `internal/stripmeta.go` | Removes immutable meta-fields (`apiVersion`, `kind`, `metadata.name`, `metadata.namespace`, `metadata.managedFields`, etc.) from all field-sets so they are never tracked |\n| `structuredMergeManager` | `internal/structuredmerge.go` | **Core leaf**: converts runtime objects to `typed.TypedValue`, calls `merge.Updater.Apply` or `merge.Updater.Update` from `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6` |\n\n### 2.2 `FieldManager` (top-level)\n\n`FieldManager` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:45`) is the public surface. It exposes:\n\n- `Update(liveObj, newObj, manager)` \u2014 called for non-apply writes (create, update, patch) to track field ownership without performing a merge.\n- `Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, manager, force)` \u2014 called for SSA apply requests; delegates into the chain and converts `merge.Conflicts` into `StatusError` with `CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict`.\n- `UpdateNoErrors(liveObj, newObj, manager)` \u2014 a fault-tolerant wrapper for `Update`; on error, clears `managedFields` rather than propagating (used by `jsonPatcher` and `smpPatcher` in the HTTP handler).\n\n### 2.3 TypeConverter\n\n`TypeConverter` (`internal/typeconverter.go:34`) bridges `runtime.Object` and `typed.TypedValue`:\n\n```go\ntype TypeConverter interface {\n    ObjectToTyped(runtime.Object, ...typed.ValidationOptions) (*typed.TypedValue, error)\n    TypedToObject(*typed.TypedValue) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\nThree implementations exist:\n\n- `typeConverter` \u2014 for built-in resources; uses a `map[GVK]*typed.ParseableType` built from the kube-openapi spec via `schemaconv.ToSchemaFromOpenAPI`.\n- `deducedTypeConverter` \u2014 for schemeless CRDs; uses `typed.DeducedParseableType`, which treats every list as atomic and every map as granular.\n- `schemeTypeConverter` \u2014 added in 2025 (`runtimetypeconverter.go`); uses the runtime `Scheme` to look up the OpenAPI definition name, allowing type conversion without a pre-built schema map.\n\n### 2.4 `GvkParser` and `internal.go` schema blob\n\n`GvkParser` (`managedfields/gvkparser.go`) maps a `GroupVersionKind` to a named type in the SMD schema, indexed from `proto.Models`.\n\nOn the client side, `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/internal/internal.go` contains a **generated** `typed.YAMLObject` schema blob for all built-in Kubernetes resource types. The `Parser()` singleton builds a `typed.Parser` from this blob once per process. Each generated per-type `Extract*` function calls `internal.Parser().Type(\"io.k8s.api.apps.v1.Deployment\")` to obtain the correct `typed.ParseableType` for extraction.\n\n### 2.5 Apply Configuration types\n\nUnder `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/<group>/<version>/` every Kubernetes kind has a generated `*ApplyConfiguration` struct (e.g., `DeploymentApplyConfiguration`). These differ from the canonical API types in one important way: **every field is a pointer** (including scalars), so that `omitempty` on JSON marshalling means \"not set by this actor\" rather than \"zero value\". This makes intent unambiguous: a nil field is absent from the apply request; the server retains whatever value is already there.\n\nTwo generated functions accompany each type:\n\n```go\n// Build from scratch\nfunc Deployment(name, namespace string) *DeploymentApplyConfiguration\n\n// Extract from live object (extract/modify-in-place/apply pattern)\nfunc ExtractDeployment(deployment *appsv1.Deployment, fieldManager string) (*DeploymentApplyConfiguration, error)\nfunc ExtractDeploymentFrom(deployment *appsv1.Deployment, fieldManager, subresource string) (*DeploymentApplyConfiguration, error)\n```\n\n`ExtractDeployment` delegates to `managedfields.ExtractInto` in `extract.go`, which reads the `FieldsV1` bitset for the named manager, calls `typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves())` via SMD, and deserialises the resulting unstructured map into the `*ApplyConfiguration` target.\n\n### 2.6 `ScaleHandler`\n\n`ScaleHandler` (`managedfields/scalehandler.go`) is a translation adapter for subresources whose field-paths differ from the parent resource. When reading `spec.replicas` through the `scale` subresource, the field is at `spec.replicas` in the parent but at `spec.replicas` in `autoscaling/v1.Scale`. `ToSubresource` projects the parent's managed field entries to the scale representation, and `ToParent` propagates changes back.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 HTTP request arrival\n\nAn SSA request arrives as `PATCH /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments/myapp` with `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml`.\n\n`PatchResource` (`handlers/patch.go:68`) reads the body, validates options, wraps admission, then dispatches on patch type:\n\n```go\ncase types.ApplyYAMLPatchType:\n    p.mechanism = newApplyPatcher(p, scope.FieldManager, yaml.Unmarshal, yaml.UnmarshalStrict)\n    p.forceAllowCreate = true\n```\n\nThe `scope.FieldManager` is a `*managedfields.FieldManager` wired up at endpoint installation time; it encapsulates the full decorator chain.\n\n### 3.2 GuaranteedUpdate loop\n\n`patchResource` sets up a transformer pipeline:\n\n```go\ntransformers := []rest.TransformFunc{p.applyPatch, p.applyAdmission, dedupOwnerReferences}\np.updatedObjectInfo = rest.DefaultUpdatedObjectInfo(nil, transformers...)\nrequestFunc = func() { p.restPatcher.Update(ctx, name, p.updatedObjectInfo, ...) }\n```\n\n`restPatcher.Update` (e.g., the generic registry's `Update`) calls `GuaranteedUpdate`, which retries the whole pipeline on conflict. On each attempt:\n\n1. **`p.applyPatch`** is called with the current live object from storage.\n2. Inside `applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject` (`patch.go:500`), the YAML body is unmarshalled into an `unstructured.Unstructured`.\n3. `p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, fieldManager, force)` is called.\n\n### 3.3 Inside `FieldManager.Apply`\n\n`FieldManager.Apply` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:183`):\n\n1. Decodes `liveObj.managedFields` via `DecodeManagedFields` into a `ManagedInterface` (a `fieldpath.ManagedFields` map + timestamp map).\n2. Calls through the decorator chain, bottom of which is `structuredMergeManager.Apply`.\n3. If the result is a `merge.Conflicts`, wraps it in a `StatusError` (`NewConflictError` in `internal/conflict.go`) with per-field `StatusCause` entries.\n4. On success, encodes the updated `ManagedInterface` back into `object.metadata.managedFields` via `EncodeObjectManagedFields`.\n\n### 3.4 Inside `structuredMergeManager.Apply`\n\n`structuredMergeManager.Apply` (`internal/structuredmerge.go:121`):\n\n1. Validates that the apply object's `GVK` matches the endpoint version.\n2. Rejects a non-nil `managedFields` in the patch object (clients may not set it).\n3. Converts `liveObj` to `typed.TypedValue` (allowing duplicates) and `patchObj` to `typed.TypedValue` (strict, no duplicates).\n4. Calls `f.updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion, managed.Fields(), manager, force)` \u2014 `f.updater` is a `merge.Updater` from `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6/merge`, which implements ownership semantics.\n5. Converts the resulting `*typed.TypedValue` back to `runtime.Object`, runs the object defaulter, and converts to the hub version.\n\n### 3.5 Conflict detection and force-apply\n\n`merge.Updater.Apply` returns `merge.Conflicts` when the incoming patch claims ownership of a field currently owned by a *different* manager. The `force` flag, passed from the client via `PatchOptions.Force`, bypasses this check and transfers ownership.\n\nThe `lastAppliedManager` layer intercepts conflicts on `kubectl` apply and filters them against fields present in `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration`: if a conflict falls entirely within the previously-owned CSA set, it silently re-applies with `force=true`. This is the migration path from client-side apply to SSA (`internal/lastappliedmanager.go:59-88`).\n\n### 3.6 Update path (non-apply writes)\n\nFor regular creates, updates, and non-apply patches, `FieldManager.Update` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:120`) is used instead of `Apply`. The `decodeLiveOrNew` helper resolves which `managedFields` to use as the starting point (live object for subresources, new object for full updates). `structuredMergeManager.Update` calls `f.updater.Update`, which tracks field changes without performing ownership merges or raising conflicts.\n\nThe `managedFieldsUpdater` layer uses a sentinel manager `\"current-operation\"` to detect whether any fields actually changed before assigning a new timestamp \u2014 an optimization preventing timestamp churn when a write is a no-op with respect to fields.\n\n### 3.7 Client-side flow: Apply functions\n\n```go\n// From doc.go example\nhpaApplyConfig := autoscalingv1.HorizontalPodAutoscaler(\"myHPA\", \"myNamespace\").\n    WithSpec(autoscalingv1.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec().\n        WithMinReplicas(1).\n        WithMaxReplicas(10).\n        WithMetrics(...)\n    )\nhpav1client.Apply(ctx, hpaApplyConfig, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"mycontroller\", Force: true})\n```\n\nThe generated `Apply` method on the typed client serialises the `*ApplyConfiguration` as JSON (with `omitempty` eliding nil fields), sends a `PATCH` with `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml`, and sets `?fieldManager=mycontroller&force=true` in the query string. The server receives only the fields explicitly set by the client.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Conflict errors\n\nA non-force apply that conflicts returns HTTP 409 with:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"message\": \"Apply failed with 2 conflicts: conflicts with \\\"other-controller\\\":\\n- .spec.replicas\\n- .spec.selector\",\n  \"status\": \"Failure\",\n  \"reason\": \"Conflict\",\n  \"details\": {\n    \"causes\": [\n      { \"reason\": \"FieldManagerConflict\", \"message\": \"conflict with \\\"other-controller\\\"\", \"field\": \".spec.replicas\" }\n    ]\n  }\n}\n```\n\nThe error is built in `internal/conflict.go:33`. Callers should inspect `errors.IsConflict(err)` and either back off, use `Force: true`, or change field ownership design.\n\n### 4.2 Manager entry cap\n\n`capManagersManager` limits update-manager entries to `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:35`). When exceeded, oldest entries (by timestamp) are merged into a per-version `\"ancient-changes\"` bucket (`internal/capmanagers.go:92`). This prevents unbounded growth of `managedFields` at the cost of losing attribution for old changes. Controllers that update objects frequently under rotating manager names (e.g., including a timestamp in the manager name) will hit this cap rapidly.\n\n### 4.3 Size pressure and managedFields removal\n\nIf an object exceeds the etcd value size limit, `patchResource` retries without `managedFields` for non-apply patch types (`patch.go:713-725`). This fallback is explicitly *not* applied to `ApplyYAMLPatchType` or `ApplyCBORPatchType` because apply semantics require the field set to be present.\n\n### 4.4 Duplicate fields\n\n`structuredMergeManager.Update` converts the live object with `typed.AllowDuplicates` because etcd may hold objects with duplicate keys (legacy data). Apply requests do not allow duplicates and fail immediately if the patch contains them (`structuredmerge.go:145`).\n\n### 4.5 No-op write optimisation\n\n`IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer` (`handlers/fieldmanager/equality.go:114`) is a write transformer that, after all mutations and admission, checks whether the only change in the new object is a timestamp bump in `managedFields`. If the object content is otherwise identical (using custom equality that ignores timestamps), the timestamps are reverted to prevent spurious `resourceVersion` increments and etcd writes. The check is opt-out via the env var `KUBE_APISERVER_AVOID_NOOP_SSA_TIMESTAMP_UPDATES=false`.\n\n### 4.6 Version-less applier identity\n\n`buildManagerInfoManager.buildManagerInfo` omits `APIVersion` from the manager key for apply operations (`buildmanagerinfo.go:63-73`). This means `kubectl` remains the same owner across a `apps/v1beta1` \u2192 `apps/v1` API version migration. Update entries, by contrast, include the API version, forming a per-version ownership footprint.\n\n### 4.7 CRD field tracking without schema\n\nFor CRDs without an OpenAPI schema, `deducedTypeConverter` treats all lists as atomic and all maps as granular. This means list items are not individually trackable; an apply that changes any list item replaces the entire list. Once a schema is added (with appropriate list-type annotations), the tracking improves. This is a fundamental limitation of schema-free CRDs.\n\n### 4.8 Subresource field isolation\n\n`FieldManager` is constructed with a `subresource` string. For subresource writes, `decodeLiveOrNew` always uses the live object's `managedFields` rather than whatever the client submits (`fieldmanager.go:83-87`). This prevents a subresource write from overwriting or corrupting the main resource's field ownership.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customisation Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 5.1 `TypeConverter` injection\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` and `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` both accept a `TypeConverter` argument. Third-party API extensions can supply their own implementation of:\n\n```go\ntype TypeConverter interface {\n    ObjectToTyped(runtime.Object, ...typed.ValidationOptions) (*typed.TypedValue, error)\n    TypedToObject(*typed.TypedValue) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\nThe `schemeTypeConverter` (`internal/runtimetypeconverter.go`) introduced in 2025 is an example; it uses `runtime.Scheme.ToOpenAPIDefinitionName` to look up the schema type, making it easier to wire SSA without a full OpenAPI spec map at construction time.\n\n**Risk**: an incorrect `TypeConverter` that misreports field types or allows unknown fields will silently corrupt ownership tracking or bypass conflict detection.\n\n### 5.2 `resetFields` filter\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` accepts a `map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter` as `resetFields`. Fields matching a filter are excluded from ownership tracking on update. This is used, for example, to prevent the apiserver from claiming ownership of fields that are reset to defaults on every write (e.g., `status` fields managed by a controller). Incorrectly configured filters can cause fields to appear unowned, allowing any applier to claim them silently.\n\n### 5.3 `ScaleHandler` for custom subresources\n\nAggregated API servers and CRD conversion webhooks that expose custom `scale` subresources use `ScaleHandler.ToSubresource` / `ToParent` to bridge field ownership between the custom resource schema and the `autoscaling/v1.Scale` schema. Registering incorrect `ResourcePathMappings` will cause replicas-ownership attribution to be lost on scale operations.\n\n### 5.4 CSA\u2192SSA upgrade utilities\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/csaupgrade/upgrade.go` provides `UpgradeManagedFields` and `UpgradeManagedFieldsPatch` for controllers migrating from client-side apply (kubectl `last-applied-configuration`) to SSA. The operation converts `Update`-operation entries for named managers into `Apply`-operation entries under a new SSA manager name. **This operation is irreversible**: the original field-level provenance is lost. Care must be taken to apply the resulting patch before any other concurrent writer changes the object.\n\n### 5.5 `UnstructuredExtractor` for dynamic clients\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/meta/v1/unstructured.go` provides an `UnstructuredExtractor` that fetches the live OpenAPI schema via discovery, builds a `GvkParser` with a 1-minute TTL, and calls `ExtractInto` to produce an `*unstructured.Unstructured` scoped to one field manager. This is the primary extension point for dynamic controllers that do not have generated typed clients.\n\n**Risk**: the TTL cache means schema changes (e.g., CRD version additions) may not be reflected immediately, causing `Extract` to use an outdated field set for up to 1 minute.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance\n\n**Object size growth**: `managedFields` in `metadata` grows with the number of distinct field managers. A single `kubectl apply` on a Deployment can add 2\u20133 KB of `managedFields` JSON. With `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10`, update churn from many distinct agents is bounded but not eliminated.\n\n**Per-request schema parsing**: The `typeConverter` is built once per `FieldManager` instance (one per kind per server) from the OpenAPI spec. During schema reloads (CRD updates), all in-flight apply operations for that kind must wait for the new `TypeConverter` to be constructed. The `schemeTypeConverter` variant avoids this by delegating to the live `Scheme`.\n\n**SMD merge complexity**: The `merge.Updater.Apply` call is O(fields \u00d7 managers). For objects with hundreds of fields and tens of managers (e.g., large Pods managed by many admission mutators), apply latency is measurable. The `CapManagersManager` is the principal mitigation.\n\n**No-op write suppression**: `IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer` prevents the common case of \"apply the same config on every reconcile loop\" from generating etcd writes, which is critical at scale.\n\n### 6.2 Reliability\n\n**`UpdateNoErrors`**: For non-apply patch types, managed field tracking failures are silently absorbed (clearing `managedFields`) rather than blocking the write. This means a storage-size-triggered or SMD-parse-triggered error degrades tracking gracefully but leaves the object without ownership information, which cannot be recovered automatically.\n\n**GuaranteedUpdate retry**: The entire `applyPatch \u2192 applyAdmission \u2192 dedup` pipeline runs inside `GuaranteedUpdate`'s retry loop. A conflict-prone object (one with many competing SSA writers) can cause many retries. Controllers should use `Force: true` and stable manager names to minimise retry pressure.\n\n### 6.3 Maintainability\n\n**Code generation**: Almost all files under `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/<group>/<version>/` and the `utils.go` dispatch table are generated by `applyconfiguration-gen`. The source of truth is the `k8s.io/api` type definitions and their JSON tags. Adding a new API field requires regenerating these packages. Handwriting an apply configuration type is an error-prone alternative.\n\n**Schema blob in `internal.go`**: The `schemaYAML` constant in `internal/internal.go` is a verbatim embedded copy of the SMD schema for all built-in types. It is regenerated as part of the release process and can become stale if the API types change between regenerations. The consequence is that `ExtractInto` may silently omit new fields that are not yet in the embedded schema.\n\n---\n\n## 7. File and Directory Map\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 internal/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 internal.go                    # Embedded SMD schema blob; Parser() singleton\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 meta/v1/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 managedfieldsentry.go          # ManagedFieldsEntryApplyConfiguration\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 unstructured.go                # UnstructuredExtractor (gvkParserCache + ExtractInto)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apps/v1/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 deployment.go                  # DeploymentApplyConfiguration; ExtractDeployment\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 utils.go                           # Dispatch table: For(obj) \u2192 *ApplyConfiguration\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 doc.go                             # (excluded by anti-requirements)\n\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 fieldmanager.go                    # Public NewDefaultFieldManager / NewDefaultCRDFieldManager\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 extract.go                         # ExtractInto: core extract-from-live logic\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 gvkparser.go                       # GvkParser: GVK \u2192 typed.ParseableType from proto.Models\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 typeconverter.go                   # TypeConverter interface re-export; NewTypeConverter, NewSchemeTypeConverter\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 scalehandler.go                    # ScaleHandler: translate managedFields for /scale subresource\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 internal/\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 manager.go                     # Manager interface (Update + Apply)\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 fieldmanager.go                # FieldManager struct; Apply / Update / UpdateNoErrors; decodeLiveOrNew\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 structuredmerge.go             # structuredMergeManager: calls sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 typeconverter.go               # typeConverter (OpenAPI-backed); deducedTypeConverter\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 runtimetypeconverter.go        # schemeTypeConverter (Scheme-backed, 2025)\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 versionconverter.go            # versionConverter: adapts runtime.ObjectConvertor for SMD\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 managedfields.go               # Encode/DecodeManagedFields; BuildManagerIdentifier\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 managedfieldsupdater.go        # managedFieldsUpdater: timestamp and delta-based ownership update\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 buildmanagerinfo.go            # buildManagerInfoManager: normalise manager key\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 capmanagers.go                 # capManagersManager: cap update entries at 10; \"ancient-changes\"\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 skipnonapplied.go              # skipNonAppliedManager: probabilistic tracking enablement\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 lastappliedmanager.go          # lastAppliedManager: CSA\u2192SSA upgrade during kubectl apply\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 lastappliedupdater.go          # lastAppliedUpdater: keep last-applied annotation in sync\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 stripmeta.go                   # stripMetaManager: exclude immutable meta fields\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 versioncheck.go                # versionCheckManager: reject wrong-version apply objects\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 conflict.go                    # NewConflictError: build StatusError from merge.Conflicts\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 pathelement.go                 # PathElement serialisation (f:, v:, k:, i: prefixes)\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 fields.go                      # FieldsToSet / SetToFields: FieldsV1 \u2194 fieldpath.Set\n\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 patch.go                           # PatchResource HTTP handler; # Server-Side Apply and applyconfigurations: A Deep Guide

## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

Server-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative ownership and merge protocol for Kubernetes objects. Rather than replacing a whole object or computing a diff client-side, SSA lets each actor (called a *field manager*) declare the fields it owns. The API server stores these ownership claims per-field in `metadata.managedFields`, and enforces them on every subsequent write.

The protocol has two tightly coupled halves:

| Half | Location | Role |
|------|----------|------|
| **applyconfigurations** (client-side types) | `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Typed, pointer-field Go structs used to build SSA requests |
| **managedfields engine** (server-side processing) | `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/` | Receives patch, performs merge, updates ownership |

### Upstream dependencies

- **`sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6`** (`merge`, `typed`, `fieldpath` packages): the authoritative merge algorithm. Kubernetes does not implement the ownership logic directly; it delegates to this external library.
- **`k8s.io/kube-openapi`** (`schemaconv`, `proto`): converts Kubernetes OpenAPI models into the schema format that `structured-merge-diff` understands. Without it, `TypeConverter` cannot annotate objects with structural type information.
- **`k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1`**: `ManagedFieldsEntry`, `PatchOptions`, `ApplyOptions` — the wire types carried in API objects and requests.

### Downstream consumers

- **`k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`**: the HTTP `PATCH` handler; routes `application/apply-patch+yaml` (and CBOR) requests to the SSA path.
- **`k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/typed/…`**: generated typed 
... (truncated)
